HTML Images Syntax

The HTML <img> tag is used to e= mbed an=20 image in a web page.

Images are not technically inserted into a web page; images are linked t= o web=20 pages. The <img> tag creates a hol= ding=20 space for the referenced image.

The <img> tag is empty, it= contains attributes only, and does not=20 have a closing tag.

The <img> tag has two required= =20 attributes:

  • src - Specifies the path to the image
  • alt - Specifies an alternate text for the image

Syntax

<img src=3D"url" alt=3D"alternatetext">

The src Attribute

The required src attribute specifies = the path (URL) to the image.

Note: When a web page loads; it is the browser, at that= =20 moment, that gets the image from a web server and inserts it into the page.= =20 Therefore, make sure that the image actually stays in the same spot in rela= tion=20 to the web page, otherwise your visitors will get a broken link icon. The b= roken=20 link icon and the alt text are shown if = the browser cannot find the image.

Example

<img src=3D"img_chania.jpg" alt=3D"Flowers=20 in Chania">
Try it Y= ourself =C2=BB

The alt Attribute

The required alt attribute provides a= n alternate text for an image, if the user for=20 some reason cannot view it (because of slow connection, an error in the src= =20 attribute, or if the user uses a screen reader).

The value of the alt attribute should= describe the image:

Example

<img src=3D"img_chania.jpg" alt=3D"Flowers=20 in Chania">
Try it Y= ourself =C2=BB

If a browser cannot find an image, it will display the value of the alt=20 attribute:

Example

<img src=3D"wrongname.gif" alt=3D"Flowers=20 in Chania">
Try it Yo= urself =C2=BB

Tip: A screen reader is a software program that reads t= he HTML code, and allows the user to "listen" to the content. Screen reader= s are useful=20 for people who are visually impaired or learning disabled.

Image Size - Width and Height

You can use the style attribute to sp= ecify the width and=20 height of an image.

Example

<img src=3D"img_girl.jpg" alt=3D"Girl in a jacket" style=3D"width:500px;height:600p= x;">
Try it Yoursel= f =C2=BB

Alternatively, you can use the width = and height attributes:

Example

<img src=3D"img_girl.jpg" alt=3D"Girl in a jacket" width=3D"500" height=3D"600">
Try it Y= ourself =C2=BB

The width and height attributes always define the width and height of the=20 image in pixels.

Note: Always specify the width and height of an image= . If width and height are not specified, the=20 web page=20 might flicker while the image loads.

Width and Height, or Style?

The width, height, and style attributes ar= e=20 all valid in HTML.

However, we suggest using the style a= ttribute. It prevents styles sheets from changing=20 the size of images:

Example

<!DOCTYPE html>
<h= tml><head>
<= ;style>
img {
  width: 100%;
}
</style>
</head&g= t;
<body>

<img src=3D"html5.gif" alt=3D"HTML5 Icon" width=3D"128" height=3D"128">

<img src=3D"html5.gif" alt=3D"HTML5 Icon" style=3D"width:128px;height:128px;">
</body>
</html>
Try it Yourse= lf =C2=BB

Images in Another Folder

If you have your images in a sub-folder, you must include the folder=20 name in the src attribute:

Example

<img src=3D"/images/html5.gif"=20 alt=3D"HTML5= Icon" style=3D"width:128px;height:128px;">
Try it Yours= elf =C2=BB

Images on Another Server/Website

Some web sites point to an image on another server.

To point to an image on another server, you must specify an absolute (fu= ll)=20 URL in the src attribute:

Example

<img src=3D"https://www.w3schools.com/images/w3schools_green.jpg" = alt=3D"W3Sch= ools.com"= >
Try it Yo= urself =C2=BB

Notes on external images: External images might be unde= r=20 copyright. If you do not get permission to use it, you may be in violation = of=20 copyright laws. In addition, you cannot control external images; it can sud= denly=20 be removed or changed.

Animated Images

HTML allows animated GIFs:

Example

<img src=3D"programming.gif" alt=3D"Computer Man" style=3D"width:48px;height:48px;"= >
Try it Your= self =C2=BB

Image as a Link

To use an image as a link, put the <img&g= t; tag inside the <a>=20 tag:

Example

<a href=3D"default.asp">
  &l= t;img src=3D"smiley.gif" alt=3D"HT= ML tutorial"=20 style=3D"wid= th:42px;height:42px;">
</a= >
Try it Yoursel= f =C2=BB

Image Floating

Use the CSS float property to let the= image float to the right or to the left of a text:

Example

<p><i= mg src=3D"smiley.gif" alt=3D"Smiley face"= style=3D"flo= at:right;width:42px;height:42px;">
The image will float to the right of=20 the text.</p>

<p><= /span><img src=3D"smiley.gif" alt=3D"Smiley face" style=3D"flo= at:left;width:42px;height:42px;">
The image will float to the left of=20 the text.</p>
Try it Yourse= lf =C2=BB

Tip: To learn more about CSS Float, read our CSS Float Tutorial.

Common Image Formats

Here are the most common image file types, which are supported in all br= owsers=20 (Chrome, Edge, Firefox, Safari, Opera):
Abbreviation File Format File Extension
APNG Animated Portable Network Graphics .apng
GIF Graphics Interchange Format .gif
ICO Microsoft Icon .ico, .cur
JPEG Joint Photographic Expert Group image .jpg, .jpeg, .jfif, .pjpeg, .pjp
PNG Portable Network Graphics .png
SVG Scalable Vector Graphics .svg

Chapter Summary

  • Use the HTML <img> element t= o define an image
  • Use the HTML src attribute to defi= ne the URL of the image
  • Use the HTML alt attribute to defi= ne an alternate text for an image, if it cannot be displayed
  • Use the HTML width and height attributes=20 or the CSS width and height=20 properties to define the size of the image
  • Use the CSS float property to let = the image float=20 to the left or to the right

Note: Loading large images takes time, and can slow d= own your=20 web page. Use images carefully.
